Organization of each data\nbase is directly related to the data to be stored; i.e.,\nnumeric data is filed in numeric order, time related data\nis filed chronologically, or alphabetic data such as\npatient names, is filed alphabetically.\t The MEDICS data\nbases can be accessed by several application programs.\nUsers use these programs to store, report, or change data\nin the data bases.\n\nI\n\nDATA CONCENTRATOR\n\nThe Data Concentrator is a software program that compacts\ndata to be sent to the Indian Health Service Computer in\nTucson.\t Another function of the Data Concentrator is to\nunpack compacted data from the computer in Tucson and transfer\nit to the terminal.\t The program also maintains the BSC line\ndiscipline for the outgoing and incoming messages.\n\nDIAL-UPS\n\nFour telephone lines are available to the user to dial the\nSTARPAHC computer for access of data.\t The user can dial\nthe computer and place the telephone headset into his terminal.\nHe then can request patient summaries from the Tucson computer p\np\t\n9.\t\nor any of the data bases maintained in the\'STARPAHC computer.\n\nDISEASE LIBRARY\n\nThis data base is a collection of reports used by the paramedics and nurses.\t The Guidelines of Care reports are used\nby the paramedics to guide them in diagnosing diseases. \t The\nNurses Standards reports are used by the nurses to remind\nt\nthem 0\'f tasks needed to be accomplished in their care of the\npatient.\t These reports are filed by Disease Name.!\'1\n\nj\n(\nI\t\n\nr\n\n\'\n\na\n\nf\n\nV\n\nt\n\nLOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMP\'ANY. INC.\n\nI \'^\n\ni\n\nSection 1\nl\n\nSUMMARY\n\nIC\n\nThe primary goals ofthe STARPAHC Program are to:\no\t\n\nProvide data for developing health care for future manned spacecraft,\n\no\t\n\nEstablish the feasibility of the STARPAHC concept for improving the\n\ndelivery of health care to remote areas on earth:\nAccordingly, the hardware and medical evaluations initiated during the first\nL:\n\nand second 6 months of system operation have been continued and expanded\nduring the third 6-month period. \t\n\nThe evaluations are based on what has\n\nproven to be a continuing stab alized 6-month period wherein system failures\n,\n\nwhich occurred during the initial shakedown period in the first 6 months\nhave been minimized.\t\n\nEarly trends and performance data reported in the\n\nprevious semi-annual reports have been reexamined to either verify, modify,\nor change earlier trends.\nThe STARPAHC Program goal is to produce, through demonstration, comprehensive\nand accurate information about the feasibility of the STARPAHC conceptas\na solution to the problem of quality health care delivery to people in remote\n\n{\n\ngeographic areas. This includes information as to the operation of a relatively\n#\n\nsophisticated "telemedicine" system functioning in a rural area. \t\n\nb\n\n(STARPAHC\n\nis at the time of this report, still the most advanced and latest technology\nof communications applied, to the health problems of the most numerous rural\npopulation anywhere in the world.) been implemented during the third\n.\'\n\n6-month period to achieve the goal of assessing the impact of STARPAHC on patient\n\ncare.\' To quantitatively evaluate the impact and assess the improvement, if any,\nbaseline data on patient visits was developed for pre-STARPAHC operation back to\nThis baseline data is compared to the one-year STARPAHC operation to deter-\n\n1970.\t\n\nmine the utilization of health services before and after STARPAHC operations.\nSpecific questions\n\nto be\n\nanswered are:\n\no\t\n\nIs the system\t improving\t accessibility to\t health care?\n\no\t\n\nIs it an improvement\n\nover the\n\npre-STARPAHC system?\n\n)3\n\nResults from studies have indicated that improved accessibility to health care\nhas been demonstrated by 1) a rate of increase in patient visits, and, (2) increase\nin ratio of patients ambulatory care visits to patients. \t Another important measure\n\ns\n\nof accessibility is that the percent of total population using services has been\nthe greatest for those more remote districts_ whose closest and most frequently\n\n#`\n\nused health service facility is the mobile health unit.\nThe changing pattern of health care, as comparedto the pre-STARPAHC system, on\n\n}\n\nthe Papago Reservation has shown an improvement in the increasing, use of physicians\'\nservices; at the Sells OPD, and an increasing use of CHM services by the Mobile,.\nClinic-served districts and the Santa Rosa district.\n{r\nThe use of telecommunications for support of the health delivery system has\n\n\'\n\ndeclined slightly during the third 6-month operation. (This is attributed to the\n\'\n\nimprovement in the datasystem permitting less contact with Medical Records at\nImprovements in the access to the health record systems obviated the\n\nf\n\nSells.)\t\n\nE\n\nneed for voice contact with Sells medical records department.\t More visits to\nSanta Rosa were for routine school examinations and for influenza immunizations\n\nM\n\ns\n\ni.\n\nwhich do not generate a need for remote consultations.\t Experience and selfconfidence gained by the CHMs is also reflected in the reduced use of tele-\n\nG\n\n}\n\nconsultations.\n\nt\nr\nS\n\nt\n\n2-1\nS\n\nLOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMPANY. INC.\n\nFurther experience in telecommunication operation was gained by adding experimental transmission of medical data via the Slow Scan TV from Sells to the\nPhoenix Indian Medical Center.\nThe specialized use of telecommunications in the transmission of images via\nSlow Scan TV for remote medical consultation was actively pursued in three\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2\t a\n\nareas:\t\n2.1\t\n\n(1) Radiology,\t (2) Skin Tones and Eye Pictures, and (3) Microscopy.\nSUMMARY OF FINDINGS IN PATTERNS OF HEALTH CARE CHANGES\nf\t\n\nThe changing pattern of health care on the Papago Reservation is a complex\npicture which varies for each district. \t\n\na\n\nThe use of the mobile clinic seems\n\nto have accelerated trends already in existence before the project started.-\n\ns\n\nAll studies have shown an increasing use of physicians\' services at the Sells\nOPD, an increasing use of CHM services by the Mobile Clinic served districts\nand the Santa Rosa district.\nHome visits mostly by Papago health program workers have also increased,\nespecially over the last year, compared with the average number of visits\n\n\'\t\n\nfor the previous two years..\t\n\nThe percent increases have been as follows:\n\nF\n\nFor the 3 western districts served by the mobile unit,, 103%; for the 2 northern\ni\t\n\ndistricts near Santa Rosa health center, 129%; for the 3 districts closest to\n\nf\t\n\nthe Sells OPD, 83%; and for the central district of Sells, 159%.\n\nt\nt\n\nIt is necessary to understand the above patterns in order to be able to relate\nquality of care study findings, and the utilization of telecommunication services.\n\nx\n\'.\n\nTwo additional studies are indicated in order to correct relative utilization\nstatistics.\t\n\n^-\n\nFirst, there is a, need to know the use of facilities outside the\n\nI\n\nreservation at the centralreferral hospital in Phoenix, and the primary clinic\nat Sacaton.\t\n\nIt is expected that this study will increase visit/population ratios\n\nfor the northern two districts, as well as revise the relative proportions of\nvisits by site, type of service, and provider categories.\nSecondly, it is necessary to know the extent to which the mobile clinic referral\npatterns accounted for both the increased use of the Sells outpatient department\nand home visits.\nv\n\n2-2\n\nt\t\n\nLOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMPANY. INC.\n\nI.\n\n; rte,\t\n\nThe greatest changes in the relative proportion of patients who receive their\nprimary care from physicians occurred in the western three districts which are\nserved by the Mobile Unit. INC.\n\nI\n\ni\ni\n\n2.6.2\t\n\n.\t\n\n,\n.\t\n\nEvaluation of Slow Scan Television - Skin Tones and Orbit Pictures,\n\nSpecific experiments were carried out in twelve_ days to determine the effectiveness of the color TV system to transmit adequate skin tones and orbital structure\nover the slow scan TV from Sells to Phoenix.\t The experiment objectives were to\nidentify/distinguish:\no Papules or macules of 3 mm diameter or less upon dark skinned individuals\no\t Scars as either raised or depressed areas\no\t Pupillary size and detail.\t\n\ns\nr\n\nLimitation of camera capabilities resulted in inadequate color differentiation\nwithin the skin tone range of hue for diagnosis of dermatological lesions . .\t The\nreal time color system \xc2\xb0does not show pap ales or macules of 3 mm diameter or less\nupon dark skinned individuals. \t The color system also fails to distinguish 4 to 5\nti\t k\nmm diameter or less red lesions in dark skinned subjects, but does transmit down\nto 3 mm lesions in fair skinned subjects.\t Streaks of cellulitis (simulated with\nred flow tip markers) 4 to 5 mm wide could not be distinguished in dark skinned\nindividuals.\n\nb\nr,\n\nr\n\nScars could not be conclusively identified as either raised or depressed areas,\nunless verbal clues were also given.\xc2\xab\nClose-up views of skin and mucoral surfaces (i.e., magnifications of 5 to 7 times)\nshowed highlighted areas with a green yellowish tinge. \t This problem was greatly\nreduced by using filters, but persisted.\n\n.\n\nSimilar difficulties were encountered in the use of slow scan color transmissions\nfor ophthalmologic problems.\t The best \'color transmissions needed to use 500 watts\nof light.\t This amount was not tolerated by the subjects.\t Excessive tearing\nresulted.\t Each tear was highlighted and the same green--yellow hue artifact was\nintroduced.`\n\nt\n\n2-30\n\nLOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMPANY, INC.\n\nThe detail of eye lids 2 lashes ., iris and scleral vessels was good ., but more\neasily achieved using the black and white system. \t Both color and black and\nwhite failed to distinguish pupillaxy site and detail in subjects with pigmented\nirises.\t Pupillaxy\t contours were easily visualized\t in blue-eyed persons.\nThe difficulty of obtaining patients with skin and eye problems ., plus the time\nneeded to transmit pictures in a room not designed for this function ., the recognized discamfort to the patients ., and the known shortcomings of the system led\nto the decision to curtail non-interactive diagnostic research in these areas.\nBoth color and black and white slow scan systems ., however., are available for\ndirect, interactive use between Sells physicians and Phoenix specialists for\ndiagnostic problems as the need arises.\n2 . 6 .3\t\nEf\n\nEvaluation of Slow Scan TV-Microscopy\n\nThe system has been adjusted to transmit adequate color images of peripheral\nblood cells at 1500 magnification.\t Double blind readings are naw in progress\nwith the objective of correct identification of white blood cell types over the\ntelevision monitor via the slow scan system.\nAttempts to transmit bacteriological specimens were not satisfactory. \t The\nreceiver in Phoenix could not distinguish gram positive (red) from gram\nnegative (purple) stained bacteria in slides with mixed flora. \t Neither could\nrod shapes be distinguished with certainty from cocci due to exceeding the\nlimits of resolution in the system.\nOther experiments in progress involve transmission of cytology slides for\ncancer screening.\n2.6.4\t\n\nEvaluation of Slaw Scan Television Summary\n\nThe use of slow scan television for.the transmission of x-ray images has indicated that the hardware performance seems to be reliable enough and the results\nachieved valuable enough to justify continued experimentation.\n\n2-31LOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMPANY, INC.\n\n.E\n\nt\t\n\n,\n\nv\n\ni.\n\nThe use of slow scan television for the transmission of patient examination\nimages has demonstrated that the-existing system requires considerable improvements in equipment, lighting, and space.\t\n\nUnder laboratory conditions, 124SC\n\nEngineering has demonstrated that (1) by using studio quality color cameras\'\nrather than the low-cost cameras presently being utilized, (2) providing studios\n\ntype balanced lighting, and (3) providing sufficient space to maneuver this\nequipment that quality transmission of color images can be achieved. \t\n\nIt is\n\nnecessary to demonstrate this in controlled clinical surroundings.\n\ns\'\n\nr\nw\n\nThe feasibility of televised microscopy from the technical viewpoint has been\nproven;\t\n\nhowever, it requires considerable experimentation.\t\n\nThe combined\n\nA\n\nproblems of optics, alignment, and color quality must be resolved. Resolution\nof this problem is the same as for patient examination -- selection of quality\nr "#\nr\n\ncolor cameras.\n,\n\nr\n\nfi\n\nk\n\ni\n\ni\n\n9\n\n\'\n\ni\n\nt\t\n\nk\n\n2-32\n\nLOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMPANY. under Project STARPAHC ., several options are under\nstudy.\t\n5.4.1\t\n\nThese includes\n\nk\n\nx\ny\n\nCost per STARPAHC Outpatient (OP) Visit\n\nThis includes the cost of treating each outpatient visit ., whether or not the\ntelecommunications system was used for each outpatient. \t\n\nOutpatients involved\n\nr:\n\nare those at the Mobile Health Unit and the Santa Rosa Clinic. ,Fluctuations in\n:,.\n\nthe number of such patients\' visits have a significant impact on such unit\n\n+\n\n4".\n\ncosts from period toperiod.\t\ni\n\n4\n\nIt is important to note that the cost per out-\n\npatient is related directly to an end production of the IndiEm Health Service.`\n\nThe unit is flexible, allowing for comparisons between different kinds of\nfacilities.\t\n\nSee Section\n\n5.5.\n\ni\n\n5.4.2\t Cost Per Hour of Operation\nAn alternative method of analysis which may be of limited specialized use\n\n^-\n\nto telecommunication planners would be cost per hour of the various systems.\nThe difference in hours of operation between the two clinics (20 hours weekly\n\nfor the Mobile Health Unit and\n\n40\n\nhours weekly for Santa Rosa) make it entries in the\nequipment usage log are (1) local surveillance, (2) surveillance during visits, and\n\n(3) review of computer printout\n\nrs\n\n-\n\ncorrelated against the system manager log, the two system\noperator\'s daily written reports, and the maintenance\n\n\'\n\ntechnician daily report.\nThe site manager oversees and routinely checks the entries on-\n\nr\n\na daily basis as part of his preparation of his daily system\nstatus report.\t\n\nSpot checking on accuracy of entries is done\n\ndirectly while observing daily occurrences.\n\nA-5\n\nt\n\nLOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMPANY, INC.\n\n`\t\n\na\n\ns\t\n\nLNSC Sunnyvale personnel, on periodic visits to the site,\nalso directly observe entries and verify accuracy on a\nsampling basis.\t\n\nThe most important surveillance is discussed continually.\t\n\nAccuracy of the entries can be verified by cross-checking\n\nthe source of information. \t\n\'\t\n\nErrors in entry have been detected\n\n3i\n\nand corrected by this means.\nA.4\t\n\nMEDICAL EVALUATION APPROACH\t\n\na\n\n.^\n\nThe purpose of this section is to provide a description of the \t\nprocedures, data sources and methods utilized in the medical\t\n\n?\n{\n\nevaluation approach.\t\nThere are some differences between the medical usage statistics\nand the hardware usage statistics.\t\n\nThis section will clarify\n\nthe reasons for these differences.\nThe primary reason for the apparent difference lies in the\ndifferent ap proaches taken b\tY medi-\t\nthe evaluation studies. \t The\nPP\t\ncal evaluation analyzes the use of the STARPAHC equipment fran \t\n;\t Y\t\n\n--\t\n\n?\n\nthe viewpoint of the impact upon patient care, whereas the hard-\n\nr\n\nware evaluation assesses the performance and use of equipment\ntypes.\nOne tool used in the medical evaluation is the analysis of each\n"patient episode" where telecommunication equipment is being \t\n\nj\n\nutilized.\nfs\n\n+i\t\n\ni\nit\t\ni3\t\nf\t\n\nThe hardware evaluation as discussed in previous sections.,\nanalyzes the use of each component of the telemedicine system.\n\n,$\n\nOne parameter is the purpose of the use of each piece of communications equipment.\t\n\nOf the six purpose categories listed,\n\n1.\n\nare related to patient services, i.e., Medical Administration\nand Clinical Consultation. \t\n\nThe two patient service purposes \t\n\n\xc2\xa2.\n\nare abbreviated as "MED/ADM" and "CHM/PHY", respectively.\n7\t\n\nA-6\n\n\xe2\x80\x9e\t\n\n_.\t\n\n.a\n\nLOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMPANY. INC.\n\n\'4\n\nA.5.5\t\n\nData Source Common to Both Evaluations (Table A-1)\n\nBoth studies utilize a computer printout titled "Equipment\nUsage Log".\t\n\nThe program is constructed from the console opera-\n\ntor\'s logs.\t\n\nIt includes the date, type of equipment used,\n\nlocations involved in the transmission, purpose of the use,\nand the quality of the signal as estimated by the operator.\n\ni\nIn one respect, the printout for the hardware evaluation differs\nfrom the printout for the medical evaluation. \t\n\nThe hardware\n\nevaluation form contains the time in minutes that each component\nwas in use.\t\n\nThe retrieval report used for medical evaluation\n\ncontains the patient\'s identification number for each use of\neach piece of communications equipment instead of the elapsed\ntime.\nA.6\t\n\n...\n\nPROCEDURES FOR ANALYSIS OF UTILIZATION REPORTS\n\nAt the end of each month ., the telecommunication evaluation forms\nr\n\nfrom the IHS staff are received by the STARPAHC evaluator.\nThe computer printout from the equipment usage logs maintained\nby the Sells systems operator is also received.\t\n\nComparisons are\n\nmade, and a list of patient transmission discrepancies is generatea and sent to the system operator.\t\n\nT\n\nThe operator then consults-\n\nthe daily hand-written logs for those transmissions reported by\nThe\n\nIHS, but not ,indicated in the equipment usage log printout. \t\n\nY\nmissing patient consults are entered into the computer if they\ncan be located in the daily log and; matched to the patient\'s\n\nidentification number.\t However, the tables prepared by the IHS\nevaluator for the monthly reports include all known patient\n\n,a\n\ntransmissions whether or not they were recorded by the systems\noperator.\nE\n\nA-16\n\nLOCKHEED MISSILES & SPACE COMPANY.
